## H. ROP / Redundancy Analysis

| Algorithm | Mean knee ROP | Mean knee selected_count | Mean front ROP | Mean front selected_count |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|
| `ar_qiea` | 0.638505 | 980.466667 | 0.503734 | 990.815534 |
| `mo_qiea` | 0.638727 | 1015.766667 | 0.575739 | 1026.469534 |
| `nsga2` | 0.657263 | 880.533333 | 0.647811 | 881.900000 |
| `random_front` | 0.662570 | 144.233333 | 0.575083 | 159.150470 |

Lower ROP means less overlap among selected tests. On this dataset, lower redundancy generally aligns with higher ETR because many tests have zero coverage over the 28 modified-line requirements. Random front tends to find smaller subsets and therefore lower overlap, while AR-QIEA and MO-QIEA produce richer fronts with more trade-off points.

## I. Statistical Analysis

| Comparison | p-value | AR wins | AR losses | Ties | Gate relation |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|---|
| `ar_qiea` vs `mo_qiea` | N/A | 30 | 0 | 0 | AR mean >= baseline mean |
| `ar_qiea` vs `nsga2` | N/A | 3 | 27 | 0 | AR mean < baseline mean |
| `ar_qiea` vs `random_front` | N/A | 0 | 30 | 0 | AR mean < baseline mean |

P1 gate result: **FAIL**.

- HV(ar_qiea) = 0.742735
- HV(mo_qiea) = 0.729753
- HV(random_front) = 0.950691
- p(ar_qiea > mo_qiea) = N/A
- p(ar_qiea > random_front) = N/A

## J. Detailed Interpretation

- Best mean HV: `random_front` with 0.950691.
- Largest mean Pareto front: `random_front` with 10.633333 points.
- Best MSR mean: `ar_qiea` with 1.000000.
- Best CGCC mean: `ar_qiea` with 1.000000.
- Best ETR mean: `random_front` with 0.957032.
- Fastest algorithm: `random_front`; slowest algorithm: `mo_qiea`.
- Paper-claim support on Lang 6b: `FAIL`. The SPEC claim requires AR-QIEA to beat MO-QIEA and random_front with statistical confidence. This run does not satisfy that gate because random_front has higher mean HV on this dataset.
- Main dataset limitation: the matrix has 2,182 zero-coverage tests against only 28 covered modified-line requirements. This makes random subset sampling unusually competitive because reducing irrelevant tests can strongly improve ETR while preserving coverage.
- Risk limitation: mutation, centrality, and execution time are P1 synthetic/proxy signals, not real Major mutation or full Java call-graph data.

## L. Reproduction Commands

Validate dataset:

```powershell
python -c "import csv,json; from pathlib import Path; p=Path('datasets/defects4j/Lang/6b'); rows=list(csv.reader((p/'matrix.csv').open(newline='',encoding='utf-8-sig'))); print(len(rows)-1, len(rows[0])-1); print(json.loads((p/'metadata.json').read_text(encoding='utf-8')))"
```

Run tests:

```powershell
$env:TEMP = (Resolve-Path '.').Path + '\.tmp'
$env:TMP = $env:TEMP
python -m pytest -q tests/test_metrics_mo.py tests/test_risk_problem.py tests/test_ar_qiea.py tests/test_nsga2.py
```

Run benchmark:

```powershell
python scripts/pareto_benchmark.py --root datasets/defects4j/Lang/6b --seeds 42..71 --pop 40 --gens 150 --algorithms ar_qiea,mo_qiea,nsga2,random_front --risk-seed 12345 --cr-threshold 0.95 --output artifacts/pareto/lang6b_full_19-06-2026.json
```

Open/view result JSON and report:

```powershell
Get-Content artifacts/pareto/lang6b_full_19-06-2026.json
Get-Content REPORT_EVERY_CHANGES/6B_Detail-Result-Analyst_19-06-2026.md
```
